  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e846da73-48ae-453f-8fff-1f61fd3ec49d'
      });
    }

    Ok, so yes. She is gay. Tui made the decision to add some LGBTQIA+ representation in the series, and it's about time. There are hints that Anemone has a crush on Tamarin, and its possible that other characters are also gay/bisexual/etc. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

<div id="review_2936615353" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2936615353" />
    <a title="Naomi Waters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87796083-naomi-waters"><img alt="Naomi Waters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599319435p2/87796083.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2936615353?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Naomi Waters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Naomi Waters" href="/user/show/87796083-naomi-waters">Naomi Waters</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87796083-naomi-waters?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87796083-naomi-waters?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87796083-naomi-waters?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2936615353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18407001891925305402">I rewrote my review.<br/>Before I get into my actual review of the book I want to add one little thing. I am sick and tired of adults posting reviews about how this book made their children uncomfortable and that they think children should be protected from the disease that is the LGBTQ community. They paint their comments and reviews like actual reviews of this book, but all they are doing is trying to cover up their homophobic ideals as an opinion that is actually worth anyone's time. Being LGBTQ+ </span>
  <span id="freeText18407001891925305402" style="display:none">I rewrote my review.<br />Before I get into my actual review of the book I want to add one little thing. I am sick and tired of adults posting reviews about how this book made their children uncomfortable and that they think children should be protected from the disease that is the LGBTQ community. They paint their comments and reviews like actual reviews of this book, but all they are doing is trying to cover up their homophobic ideals as an opinion that is actually worth anyone's time. Being LGBTQ+ isn't disgusting, and you can't protect your children from something that isn't something they should be protected from. I knew I liked girls when I was 8 years old, I didn't know what homosexual meant, I didn't know what gay or lesbian meant. I was an 8 year old child that kissed my best friend and was bullied because of it. My child brain told me that the reason everyone hated me was because I kissed a girl, so I spent the next several years burying myself so deep in denial that I convinced myself I liked boys; all that did was throw me into one abusive relationship after another. It took me until I was 17 years old to realize I did like girls, it took me another year to stop being disgusted with myself. I was a "protected" child, it didn't protect me from anything, it just made me hate myself, and then it made me hate my parents. <br />The only thing I hated about this book was what was done to Tsunami. She did not feel like Tsunami to me at all, and just didn't act like herself whatsoever. I was greatly disappointed by what was done with her. Honestly Sutherland did not need to put Tsunami and Turtle in this book at all. They weren't used, they didn't do anything, and they weren't written like they should have been. I mean we get to see them so little that they don't even feel like real characters in this book. If they hadn't been put into this novel then I would have adored it because I love Sundew. But Tsunami is my baby, and what Sutherland did with her just ruined this entire book for me. <br />Okay I feel like my original review of this book was way to harsh. Will I up the rating? Nope, it still gets 2.5 stars from me. But I am rewriting some of my review because I did love some parts of this book. I loved Sundew and Willow's relationship, I loved Leafwing culture, I loved Hazel, and Bumblee is just the best little babu. Now please don't think I loved Sundew being gay because I want to jump on the hype train. I loved that aspect of the book because it told me and my girlfriend that it is okay to be who we are. Neither of us have told our parents about our relationship because we are terrified of how they would react. But this book gave us the courage to come clean about we we are, and that we love each other.<br />And hey if you are homophobic I just want to say.... that you are wrong and you don't have a single right to feel the way you do. So jump in a hole and stay there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18407001891925305402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2949181900" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2949181900" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7149688-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517457940p2/7149688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2949181900?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/7149688-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2949181900" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6975583219164363243">This book broke my heart and not in a good way. I have a classroom and encourage elementary school readers to check out books from my personal library to help kids find books they like. I, and they, have, up until now LOVED this series and I would buy the newest edition as soon as it was released every time. Sadly, the author chose to include same sex partners in this book and I and my school decided that we will no longer be encouraging these books. I am heartbroken because I love this series a</span>
  <span id="freeText6975583219164363243" style="display:none">This book broke my heart and not in a good way. I have a classroom and encourage elementary school readers to check out books from my personal library to help kids find books they like. I, and they, have, up until now LOVED this series and I would buy the newest edition as soon as it was released every time. Sadly, the author chose to include same sex partners in this book and I and my school decided that we will no longer be encouraging these books. I am heartbroken because I love this series and the writing style is engaging and clever, but I do not condone introducing this particular subject to children of such a young age. Kids today are being hammered about their sexuality at far to young an age and sadly this appears to be another attempt to cozy up to the minority group that is trying to force feed a specific agenda. Now, this is MY review, not anyone else's so each person has to make their own choices and this is why I made mine. Unfortunately, this author is so good at writing that once she introduces a character, she will bring them up in most of the books. So, I can't even skip this one book and go on with the series, because now the characters are cannon. I accept that others may feel different, but this series will no longer have a place in my classroom and with so much regret, I have to pass. I am NOT against people who are attracted to the same sex, but I AM against forcing children who are not emotionally, physically, or mentally ready for the topic of sexuality to be exposed before they even know who THEY are.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6975583219164363243" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2747002157" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2747002157" />
    <a title="Makena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75701398-makena"><img alt="Makena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561789072p2/75701398.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2747002157?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Makena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Makena" href="/user/show/75701398-makena">Makena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2747002157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11966741902472039052">EDIT: Looking back at this a few months later, I realized that I sound a lot more heated than I probably should. However, I still stand behind my review. Please look at the context before you claim I disliked it simply because it "had a lesbian in it." I gave several reasons as to why the book was poorly executed. If you would like to ask about my stance, please do so cordially.<br/><br/>2.3 stars. <br/><br/>Let me start off by saying: I love this series. The characters are unique and fun, likewise with the stories</span>
  <span id="freeText11966741902472039052" style="display:none">EDIT: Looking back at this a few months later, I realized that I sound a lot more heated than I probably should. However, I still stand behind my review. Please look at the context before you claim I disliked it simply because it "had a lesbian in it." I gave several reasons as to why the book was poorly executed. If you would like to ask about my stance, please do so cordially.<br /><br />2.3 stars. <br /><br />Let me start off by saying: I love this series. The characters are unique and fun, likewise with the stories themselves. The few who have seen my previous reviews know that I often give the books a raving five stars. However, with that said, I can confidently say that I have never before been so disappointed by a book in my life. <br /><br />Let me just lay down the backdrop: In the previous books, we were given fantastic escapes, lovely characters, and fascinating stories where dragons were fleeing prisons, stealing sacred artifacts, and hiding from the evil law of the land. They really gripped you and kept you reading. Then this book came along, and we got... some plants. Instead of daring escapes, we got wandering around in a jungle. Instead of fascinating stories, we got some filler and approximately two plot twists. And, on top of it all, instead of a fun band of heroes to follow, we were stuck with flat old Sundew, whilst the others were thrown under a bus.<br /><br />But, let's give Sundew the benefit of the doubt. I mean, she's a strong-willed, independent female. <br /><br />Oh, and she's lesbian.<br /><br />This trope has quickly become an aggravating cliché in our culture today. Not to mention the fact that practically EVERY OTHER CHARACTER IN THIS SERIES ALREADY HAS A LOVE INTEREST. I mean, really, could we please have just one dragon who's not mooning over someone or other? <br /><br /> Frankly, I felt betrayed. As a Christian, I believe homosexuality to be a sin. Does that mean I hate all those who practice it? No. However, it does mean that having it blatantly shoved into a book for no reason other than to look more "with the times' feels like a slap in the face. Especially since the author is constantly reminding you that "oh yeah, she's the only dragon for her" and "oh look how cute they are together," and "only the annoying dragons give a rip about their relationship." Sundew quickly became just a puddle of mush. Her thought process throughout the book went in circles: "Willow's the only dragon for me" "My mom makes me so mad" "The HiveWings make me so mad." In short, she just felt mad all the time. It made for a very boring character in general. Sutherland's constant reminder of the fact that the two dragons were, in fact, going to get married was only slightly subtler than a kick in the pants. The message I heard sounded like: "I know I'm angering about 50% of my readership, but this is happening, and there's nothing they can do to stop it. Just accept it." I get enough of that in practically every other outlet -- must I read about it in a middle grade novel about dragons?<br /><br />Putting aside just how weird the relationship felt, it just added a layer of awkwardness to everything, not to mention the complete unnecessity of it all. Sure, we got to see a different side of Sundew, but it didn't add much to the story. Not to mention the fact that Willow (the love interest) came off dull and annoying, basically another Sunny clone. I mean, why would Sundew, of all characters, be disappointed by the fact that Willow didn't introduce Dew to her father as her "girlfriend?"<br /><br />And that's just Sundew's problem. The rest of the characters (save Cricket, to an extent) were barely heard during the entire novel. Plus, the new characters were stock and bland. Just a bunch of grumpy soldiers, which sound just like Skywings. In short, we got no character development whatsoever.<br /><br />We haven't even talked about the plot. I mean, how many times must we read about some daring escape from a carnivorous plant? These were boring and just felt like filler. Seriously, there were two just within a few paragraphs of each other. There was no plot tension whatsoever, and it only got interesting near the end. The plot moved about as fast as some of those plant conversations we had to listen in on.<br /><br />So, in conclusion to my ill-written rant, I'll pose a question to Mrs. Sutherland: was one political statement worth the quality of her writing and the alienation of hundreds of readers?</span>
  <a data-text-id="11966741902472039052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2826388427" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2826388427" />
    <a title="Rebel Rider" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17457849-rebel-rider"><img alt="Rebel Rider" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521134835p2/17457849.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2826388427?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebel Rider" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebel Rider" href="/user/show/17457849-rebel-rider">Rebel Rider</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17457849-rebel-rider?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17457849-rebel-rider?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17457849-rebel-rider?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17457849-rebel-rider?shelf=lgtb">lgtb</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2826388427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16285631829569857142">Guys, I found it. A love story worse than Twilight.<br/>The book started okay, but about a third of the way through, it turns out the main character, a girl dragon, has a girlfriend who is her one true love. I have some beliefs that mean I don't think that sort of relationship should be promoted, so this bothered me, especially since so much of the book was about it.<br/>Now, not only does she have a girlfriend, but in a flashback, we find out it was love at first sight when Sundew was TWO YEARS OLD. I kn</span>
  <span id="freeText16285631829569857142" style="display:none">Guys, I found it. A love story worse than Twilight.<br />The book started okay, but about a third of the way through, it turns out the main character, a girl dragon, has a girlfriend who is her one true love. I have some beliefs that mean I don't think that sort of relationship should be promoted, so this bothered me, especially since so much of the book was about it.<br />Now, not only does she have a girlfriend, but in a flashback, we find out it was love at first sight when Sundew was TWO YEARS OLD. I know dragons age faster than humans, but two is still way too young for love at first sight, and it seems like the other dragon was older too. Not only that, this dragon sparkled like a Twilight vampire. (I'm not joking. She's sparkly in the flashback.) <br />The author goes to great extents to normalize gay dragons, to the point no one seems that upset about it, other than a couple glares. Sundew was supposed to marry another dragon because she and he share certain powers. The fact that Sundew is lesbian should cause some issue because, logically, that means she wouldn't be passing on her genetics, which is apparently a big enough deal that she'd have been put in a forced marriage to produce little dragons that talk to plants. This fact that everyone's plan for breeding dragons is ruined isn't mentioned, even though it should have caused a huge blow up.<br />The writing is also somewhat annoying. The romance is a huge focus of the storyline, and the romantic interest, Willow, has no real personality, other than being the opposite of the main character. Normally, Tui's characters are interesting, but Willow's pretty flat. It's obvious that, so far, her only role in the storyline is "Sundew's girlfriend." While Cricket is an interesting character and is often doing things, Willow would have no real role without Sundew.<br />And then the third thing. These dragons keep walking through this dragon eating poison jungle. I don't remember anyone mentioning why they can't simply climb a tall tree, then fly over the jungle. Did dragon wings somehow stop working along with dragon magic?<br /><br />Overall, I don't see why pre-teens should have books that are full of romance, no matter what gender the characters are. Kids don't read books about dragons because they want dragons touching claws and tails and wings. Romance shouldn't be a big focus of stories geared toward this age group, especially stories that are supposed to be about adventure and dragons.<br />I miss the original series. That had a lot more action and fun in it, and the romance wasn't nearly as much of a focus. It seems to be going downhill badly. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16285631829569857142" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2475627389" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2475627389" />
    <a title="Annie (Putt)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47291796-annie-putt"><img alt="Annie (Putt)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582160152p2/47291796.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2475627389?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie (Putt)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie (Putt)" href="/user/show/47291796-annie-putt">Annie (Putt)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2475627389" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1973717985986631189">So this was boring.<br/><br/>I went into this with such high hopes and I think, with how much the plot got derailed for romance, I kinda want to lower the ratings on the other Wings of Fire books too because this has been a consistent problem with this series, and I'm sick of it.<br/><br/>Sundew was an amazing character but, for whatever reason, her character development got completely swept aside. She's a strong and calculating dragon. She understood risks and how to prepare for basically anything, <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[</span></span>
  <span id="freeText1973717985986631189" style="display:none">So this was boring.<br /><br />I went into this with such high hopes and I think, with how much the plot got derailed for romance, I kinda want to lower the ratings on the other Wings of Fire books too because this has been a consistent problem with this series, and I'm sick of it.<br /><br />Sundew was an amazing character but, for whatever reason, her character development got completely swept aside. She's a strong and calculating dragon. She understood risks and how to prepare for basically anything, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[yet for whatever reason in this story she thought it was OK to take a freaking baby dragonet into the horrible dark depths of the jungle where she was almost eaten <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I get Tui wanted to write the conflict between her and her mom, but OH MY GOSH it was exhausting. Sundew felt like a cliche teenager rebelling instead of calculated like she had before.<br /><br />There also felt to be very little stakes in this. The ending had a lot of big things happening, but all of the major stuff that had been built up over the last two books happened to all the characters off page, so it didn't really matter because they weren't the main ones in the story because we were off with Sundew legitimately doing nothing. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The fact that my poor friend has had to listen to me rant for an hour about the ending of this book should be an indication of how frustrated I was. A PLANT??? Your big bad is a scary, evil plant. What a great way to discount literally every bit of development and complexity built up into the last two books, Tui. What a wonderful way to make the genocide of the LeafWings a JOKE. Because an evil plant made them do it. All the applause. Much wow. Pardon the salt, but this made me mad. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />This could have been a phenomenal story about the effects of war, genocide, and how one comes back from that. Willow proved you could. Sundew proved you could, if we're to take any of her development seriously from the other two books, and yet Sundew takes such a big step backwards in this that any hope for a compelling plot of dragon versus dragon and trying to understand why good people do bad things is now completely gone. You know what I wanted? All the vibes of the new <i>She Ra</i> TV series. Something that has goofy moments that is juxtaposed with seriousness. Cute couples and real challenges. We got the cute couples bit, but, as I said earlier, no stakes in this story. We got the goofiness, but it felt forced and out of place. Seriousness? Yeah, no. Sorry, I can't buy the storyline.<br /><br />As of now, I am officially DNFing this story, as the more I think of it, the less it appeals to me. Sundew could have been great if Sundew had acted the same as she was in Hive Queen. But she was worse than she ever behaved in any of the previous books, and so her story flopped. If Sutherland had made this book about Willow, it would have been more compelling because at least Willow was a good character. I wanted the rough, hardened character of Sundew with her gentle, firm girlfriend/bff and this would have been a solid 4 star book. Or just make this from Willow's POV and less time in Sundew's head woulda been great too.<br /><br />And if you like this book, no sarcasm comes from me when I say this: I'm glad. This is a beautiful world with amazing dragons, a diverse cast of characters with mental illness and relationships. I wish I liked it more. I really, really do, but I'm sick and tired of series getting dragged out because they make money and authors being too afraid to do gritty topics with Middle Grade and YA.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1973717985986631189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2980321591" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2980321591" />
    <a title="Pamelia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5234530-pamelia"><img alt="Pamelia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517814782p2/5234530.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2980321591?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pamelia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pamelia" href="/user/show/5234530-pamelia">Pamelia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2980321591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1152751855268007287">Parents: if your preferred method of educating your elementary aged child about same sex attraction includes sympathizing with a character that alternates between hating her parents and unhealthily obsessing about her crush, sneaking out to make-out with said crush, and generally acting out in an out of control rebellious disrespectful manner then this is the book for you! <br/>My daughter, who has read all of the books in this series, came to me tonight to tell me that this book made her feel uncomf</span>
  <span id="freeText1152751855268007287" style="display:none">Parents: if your preferred method of educating your elementary aged child about same sex attraction includes sympathizing with a character that alternates between hating her parents and unhealthily obsessing about her crush, sneaking out to make-out with said crush, and generally acting out in an out of control rebellious disrespectful manner then this is the book for you! <br />My daughter, who has read all of the books in this series, came to me tonight to tell me that this book made her feel uncomfortable and that she doesn’t want to finish it. <br />She is disappointed and ‘sad that the author had to ruin it, it doesn’t feel right and makes me uncomfortable’. She struggled with the author's choice to have Sundew constantly hating her mother and obsessing over Willow. She wasn't prepared for an angsty lesbian romance with a rebellious hate-filled main character. Neither of us were aware of or prepared for the direction this book took. <br />Kids have so much coming at them these days. I am so tired of it. Where has the simplicity of childhood gone. No one is concerned with preserving innocence. It’s like a race to get children indoctrinated and ‘woke’ before their parents can turn them into little bigots. <br />It is infuriating as a parent that everyone with a platform feels the need to add their voice to the noise coming at my children. <br />This book definitely sparked some in-depth conversations with my child. We discussed how when you read an author’s book you’re inviting them and their ideas into your head space. And when that author presumes to take you places you don’t want to be and they weren’t up front about the destination in the first place, you are not obligated to let them camp out in your head. Move on, there is no rule about finishing a series once you’ve started it.<br />It isn’t a mistake or an oversight that the author and this book’s publishers have omitted the details of the story’s direction and Sundew’s big romance in the synopsis. If this book’s content is something that’s acceptable, why are they mum about it in the book’s description?</span>
  <a data-text-id="1152751855268007287" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781338214512" href="/book/show/41473825-the-poison-jungle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22027176-connor?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22027176-connor?shelf=middle-grade-high-fantasy">middle-grade-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22027176-connor?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2780341148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6918099910560666712">I'm continuing to really enjoy this arc of the series! I really loved seeing the poison jungle and all the carnivorous plants that want to eat everything and everyone. Bumblebee is the cutest. I really liked the differences between the LeafWing groups as well. The differences in the different cultures of the dragons on this continent are so varied and interesting. Additionally, I like that the LGBT+ characters are no longer just in the background (Clay's brother, Umber, had a crush on Qibli in b</span>
  <span id="freeText6918099910560666712" style="display:none">I'm continuing to really enjoy this arc of the series! I really loved seeing the poison jungle and all the carnivorous plants that want to eat everything and everyone. Bumblebee is the cutest. I really liked the differences between the LeafWing groups as well. The differences in the different cultures of the dragons on this continent are so varied and interesting. Additionally, I like that the LGBT+ characters are no longer just in the background (Clay's brother, Umber, had a crush on Qibli in book 6, and more LGBT+ side characters have been introduced since then. Side note: I want to see Umber again!) It's nice to see two female dragons together. <br /><br />However, I think this might be my least favorite of this arc so far. While the previous books focus on working together to overcome adversity, this one drops that somewhat. The group takes a backseat to Sundew's relationship with Willow, and I agree with some of the criticisms on that front. Sundew's characterization changes rapidly once Willow is brought into the picture. Don't get me wrong, there are a lot of people that act completely different when with their partners versus when they're with others. But Sundew's whole personality seems to shift and was different than the previous books. I can see the arguments on both sides. Sundew was away from home and maybe didn't have Willow at the forefront of her mind while trying to dodge crazy HiveWings, but she really is sooo different once Willow is around. <br /><br />Also, I think Tsunami seemed a bit off in this book. She doesn't seem very much like the Tsunami that I knew in the previous books, so I hope some of her old self is brought back in the next book. I did enjoy this one, and I hope Sundew recovers some more of her acerbic dialogue back in the future books because I find it hilarious!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6918099910560666712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2916769088" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2916769088" />
    <a title="Rebecca H." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/85580239-rebecca-h"><img alt="Rebecca H." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557668089p2/85580239.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2916769088?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca H." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca H." href="/user/show/85580239-rebecca-h">Rebecca H.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2916769088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1414140478512904309">Another thrilling installment in my all-time favorite series! It wasn't by any means perfect, but Sundew and our band of protagonists make this one of the most enjoyable books I've read.<br/><br/>Now, let's start with the good. Sundew is an extremely fun PoV character to read about. She reminds me of Peril in all the right ways, but she's still very much unique and her own dragon.<br/><br/>Bumblebee is the most adorable fictional child I've ever met. She can be both annoying and endearing at the same time, which is</span>
  <span id="freeText1414140478512904309" style="display:none">Another thrilling installment in my all-time favorite series! It wasn't by any means perfect, but Sundew and our band of protagonists make this one of the most enjoyable books I've read.<br /><br />Now, let's start with the good. Sundew is an extremely fun PoV character to read about. She reminds me of Peril in all the right ways, but she's still very much unique and her own dragon.<br /><br />Bumblebee is the most adorable fictional child I've ever met. She can be both annoying and endearing at the same time, which is a difficult balance to find. Sundew warming up to her is a gradual process that makes for some wonderful moments of character development.<br /><br />The jungle itself is a fascinating setting. I get the feeling we've only seen a snippet of it, as the writing makes it seem so vast and alive. I look forward to finding out more about it and the history of Pantala over the next two books.<br /><br />The writing style, of course, never ceases to impress. How Tui can so distinctly capture each dragon's personalities in even the simplest of descriptions always leaves me wanting more. It draws you right in and won't let you put the book down for long. <br /><br />The emotional beats were all on-point. I felt nervous when the characters were in danger, and felt the unease and sadness right alongside Sundew when the realities of going to war really struck her. Finally, getting to see Tsunami and Turtle (two of my all-time favorite characters) again was quite a treat. Just reading their names again got my heart pounding with excitement.<br /><br />Okay, now for the bad. There will be spoilers from here on out, so if you haven't read the book yet, go do that first, then come back and read this, if you're still interested. For your own safety, the rest of this review (minus my final thoughts) has been hidden.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[First off, leafspeak magic and the fact that plants can even speak at all was a little strange and took me out of the book more than once. However, for what it was, it was certainly handled well. It also left me wondering if all plants in this universe can talk and/or feel, which isn't bad; it's just a funny thing to think about. <br /><br />The biggest problem I had with the whole leafspeak and talking plants story element was how Hawthorne and everyone else were all essentially mind controlled by some ivy. That's right; as far as we know at the end of this book, the ultimate villain of this arc is . . . a plant. I have no clue what to think about this, and that's really all I can say about it.<br /><br />Even though it's the story that has been told and built on since the beginning of the arc, I still really don't want Clearsight to have split up the "Beetlewings" into two tribes. It just seems like there should be so much more to the tribes' history than that. There are so many possibilities having nothing to do with Clearsight, and I'll be mildly disappointed if nothing comes along and changes up the story. But as with all of the negatives I'm listing here, this is just a personal gripe.<br /><br />And lastly, that epilogue. This isn't really a negative, but I'm guessing this means Jerboa has ended animus magic. I'll admit, I'd come up with some pretty wild theories about what was happening with animus magic, including the possibility of Anemone making Tamarin an animus while trying to cure her blindness, and Tamarin enchanting animus magic away. There was certainly enough foreshadowing for it to be a possibility. Jerboa being the cause of its disappearance makes sense, but it is a tad underwhelming. I can't help but wonder if it's gone forever, or if it'll somehow get replaced by a magic system with rules. Given the number of Leafwings about to swarm Pyrrhia, perhaps something having to do with potion-making will come into play, which would be a pretty interesting development. But now I'm getting more into speculations and theories than the book itself.<br /><br />Now I just need to know who the next book is going to follow and how the dragons of Pyrrhia are going to react to all of these newcomers appearing on their shores. Whatever path the next book takes, it's going to be one heck of a ride. I look forward to experiencing it. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />In summary, <i>The Poison Jungle</i> is a fairly solid book in a stellar series, and I don't foresee many fans being let down by it in any meaningful way. <b>4/5—Go read it!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1414140478512904309" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2804831881" />
    <a title="Miranda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/96572336-miranda"><img alt="Miranda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604850239p2/96572336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2804831881?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda" href="/user/show/96572336-miranda">Miranda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2804831881" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17300193988448703856">Spoilers Ahead!<br/>The two best parts of this book, in my opinion, has to be the setting and the characters. <br/><br/>The Poison Jungle... it has a nice ring to it. If i were a Leafwing (Sapwing? Poisonwing?) I would totally give my home a scary name. Not only because its fun to freak out Hivewings, it will keep those Hivewings and Silkwings away. <br/>The Poison Jungle is full of carnivorous plants that are hungry for a big, juicy meal of stupid dragons *cough* Swordtail *cough* and are amazing at adapting to su</span>
  <span id="freeText17300193988448703856" style="display:none">Spoilers Ahead!<br />The two best parts of this book, in my opinion, has to be the setting and the characters. <br /><br />The Poison Jungle... it has a nice ring to it. If i were a Leafwing (Sapwing? Poisonwing?) I would totally give my home a scary name. Not only because its fun to freak out Hivewings, it will keep those Hivewings and Silkwings away. <br />The Poison Jungle is full of carnivorous plants that are hungry for a big, juicy meal of stupid dragons *cough* Swordtail *cough* and are amazing at adapting to suit their needs. For example, they have a hard shell and grow near each other so dragons can't free their poor idiotic friend trapped in the plant. I never knew plants could be so smart.<br />I also enjoyed the different plant life mentioned in the book, such as greenbriar, sundew, or my persal favorite, "...a promising kudzu vine choking one of the trees...". For those of you reading who don't know what kudzu is, its a super invasive plant. Look it up.<br /><br />Next I'll mention my absolute favorite part of the book, characters. Tui did an amazing job with the character's personalities and character developement. <br />Let's begin with some of our characters we've known forever. Blue, Cricket, and Swordtail. I admit I'm frustrated Blue just got shoved out of the adventure. I was dying to see him be eaten by a plant. But I still understand why he couldn't come along on the journey to Hawthorn. Since he can't use his flamesilk in the jungle or everything will catch fire, he became useless. Cricket just is the annoying one who talks and asked questions all the time, so she hasn't changed. Swordtail seemed to be there because Sundew needed someone to yell at and the team needed someone to rush into things and get eaten. Overall, these three didn't really change in personality at all. <br />Now its time for the main character, Sundew. She managed to evolve as a character but still be the independent, angry Sundew we know and love. Sundew also has a kind of relationship thats a bit different from all the other romances in the series. She has a girlfriend. I have no arguments against it. In fact, Willow and Sundew are cute together. Every time they shared a cute moment, like wrapping their tails around each other, I kept hoping for some sappy conversation. Nope. They don't need to talk to each other. Their relationship just works. I still wish Willow and Sundew had some of those heart to heart conversations just so readers could see a more vulnerable Sundew. <br />Last, but not least, Bumblebee. She is the best at comic relief. She's also incredibly smart. Bumblebee reminds me of Sunny from Series of Unfortunnate Events. Anyone agree? But I love that cute dragonet. <br /><br />Overall this book is amazing. Id recommend it to all my friends. And if I could say something to any future characters, my advice would be to always let Swordtail go first.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17300193988448703856" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2954872308" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer18415846892386950411"><strong>A Broken Fan</strong><br/><br/>This one will be long...I apologize. <br/><br/> So I read the first book about a month after it released. To be short...I loved it. As did I love every book till the fifth. At the end of the fifth I thought it was done, and I was ok with that. Then Six drops with Moonwatcher and that one too was great. From that point on I started a personal tradition, every time a new book come out I reread the whole series from book one all the way to the new book. Book ten drops and I keep this up. I hear o</span>
  <span id="freeText18415846892386950411" style="display:none"><strong>A Broken Fan</strong><br /><br />This one will be long...I apologize. <br /><br /> So I read the first book about a month after it released. To be short...I loved it. As did I love every book till the fifth. At the end of the fifth I thought it was done, and I was ok with that. Then Six drops with Moonwatcher and that one too was great. From that point on I started a personal tradition, every time a new book come out I reread the whole series from book one all the way to the new book. Book ten drops and I keep this up. I hear of book 11 and I reread the whole series again. I still loved those 10. 11 I liked, but kind of. Blue to me was such a whimp. I know that is for story and hats his character, and I understand and in fact it's better for long term plot. I get that. 12 comes and I love Cricket too. I finish 12 and eventually hear of 13, so I reread it all again. Then...Sundew....<br /> I loved Sundew. She was the badass who was small and intimidating. She reminded me of Darkstalker, who is my favorite dragon of all time from anything. But...find out she has a girlfriend and I lose my mind. I myself am a bit of a scientific person...so a gay dragon made me completely lose my love for the character. Heh here I am saying I am scientific person who loves books about dragons...yea sue me. <br /> I truly felt back stabbed by this book. I felt Clay prove himself as a protector. I felt Tsunami prove she can control herself. I felt Glory become queen. I felt Starflight's understanding of the Nightwings. I felt Sunny become a hero. I felt DarkStalker's pain and suffering. I felt So many emotions from these books...I can go on and on.<br /> But...not this book...this book did not make me want to know more...I feel like a broken fan...<br />And to those who a pose my views...I apologize for having a opinion. I forget that people can be offended by mere thoughts. <br /> Tui...I'm sorry...but...I need a break...I will reread 1-12....but not 13 for many time to come.<br /> -With sadness, A Broken Fan</span>
  <a data-text-id="18415846892386950411" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14735661320993301298">I loved this book so much! I loved how you got to learn more about Sundew's character. I've read reviews that say it's nothing like Sundew, she's too independent, but I think it's perfect. Why? She's independent, yes, but that means she's not open to other dragons, which means she can be nasty or secretive. This is why we thought she was a mean dragon.   <span id="freeText14735661320993301298" style="display:none">I loved this book so much! I loved how you got to learn more about Sundew's character. I've read reviews that say it's nothing like Sundew, she's too independent, but I think it's perfect. Why? She's independent, yes, but that means she's not open to other dragons, which means she can be nasty or secretive. This is why we thought she was a mean dragon. She keeps her true personality secret from others because she's afraid of how it might affect their relationship. She is sort of feisty, but at the same time cares very much for Willow. Willow calms her down and let's her see that she doesn't have to fight everyone and murder them all. This is a great book and I completely disagree with people saying that Sundew's personality is wrong.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2922764913" />
    <a title="Allegra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77175824-allegra"><img alt="Allegra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528145161p2/77175824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2922764913?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allegra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allegra" href="/user/show/77175824-allegra">Allegra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2922764913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16633732700502905256">I always love the little twists that Sutherland throws into the Wings of Fire books so I was really looking forward to how the twist would come about in this one and it was incredibly fun! To get out the negative first, I was mildly annoying with the way in which she wrote about Sundew's anger. Of course these are made up creatures in a made up world but the themes of this world very clearly relate to ours and having an author who doesn't completely understand the emotions of people who are oppr</span>
  <span id="freeText16633732700502905256" style="display:none">I always love the little twists that Sutherland throws into the Wings of Fire books so I was really looking forward to how the twist would come about in this one and it was incredibly fun! To get out the negative first, I was mildly annoying with the way in which she wrote about Sundew's anger. Of course these are made up creatures in a made up world but the themes of this world very clearly relate to ours and having an author who doesn't completely understand the emotions of people who are oppressed write about a large group that are oppressed was...not smooth in some areas. She came from a positive place, wanting to understand but I feel that there were a few hiccups with this.<br />Other than this I love that Sutherland is always willing to provide representation with different family dynamics. A daughter/mother relationship that doesn't workout, a fierce lesbian with a sweet lesbian both helping each other through their emotions, and an arranged marriage for the sake of their tribe. It's incredibly refreshing and certainly a highlight. The other highlight being the lively dialogue between characters. Sutherland always manages create such unique, funny protagonists in all her novels. It's really wonderful.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16633732700502905256" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2954878709" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3277072821381648052">These books just seem to keep getting better. I wish they weren't published so far apart but then again every 6 months to a year is still incredibly quick. The relationship building for this age group of book is astounding and I love all of the characters. Twists keep coming that are usually surprising even to those of us who are not the target audience. Finally some good dragon books WITHOUT the need for humans as a main drive. Love this series, can't wait to keep reading it as more come out. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3003708203" />
    <a title="Karissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4057501-karissa"><img alt="Karissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557318686p2/4057501.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3003708203?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karissa" href="/user/show/4057501-karissa">Karissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3003708203" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14374038774773646110">This is the 13th book in the Wings of Fire series, the third book taking place on the new continent of Pantala. I enjoyed this a lot, this was a great continuation of the Wings of Fire series.<br/><br/>This book follows Sundew as she tries to help overthrow the HiveWings while protecting and supporting her new friends. We also get to interact with some wonderful dragons from the Old Continent.<br/><br/>This book was really fun to read. I mainly read these because my son loves them and loves talking to me about them</span>
  <span id="freeText14374038774773646110" style="display:none">This is the 13th book in the Wings of Fire series, the third book taking place on the new continent of Pantala. I enjoyed this a lot, this was a great continuation of the Wings of Fire series.<br /><br />This book follows Sundew as she tries to help overthrow the HiveWings while protecting and supporting her new friends. We also get to interact with some wonderful dragons from the Old Continent.<br /><br />This book was really fun to read. I mainly read these because my son loves them and loves talking to me about them. However, if I am being honest I end up really loving them every time I read them. I loved the adventure through the Poison Jungle and Sundew’s snarky attitude. Sutherland is always spot on with her dialogue and gets me laughing out loud a number of times. I can’t think of another author that does such great and humorous dialogue and makes her dragons seem so...real.<br /><br />This book finally sees the two worlds colliding (old and new continents) and we learn a ton of really intriguing history about Pantala. I really loved it.<br /><br />Overall I loved this and think fans of the Wings of Fire series will be really pleased. This is a series I think all ages can really get into; it’s very well written and highly entertaining. My son and I love this series and it just keeps getting better.<br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2917660101" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2917660101" />
    <a title="ARS" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31328248-ars"><img alt="ARS" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589410155p2/31328248.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2917660101?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ARS" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ARS" href="/user/show/31328248-ars">ARS</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2917660101&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2917660101" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15853628448028109822"><strong>I don’t even know where to start.</strong><br/><br/>Okay, so first: the bad. <br/>Whenever I first started this book, I was worried that it wouldn’t further the third arc’s plot quickly enough. By the end, though, it felt just a *teensy bit* too fast.<br/>Also, Turtle didn’t get nearly as much spotlight as he deserved, but that’s just a nitpick coming from a Turtle fanboy.<br/><br/>And that’s it! Onto the good:<br/>SUNDEW AND WILLOW ARE SO FLIPPING ADORABLE! And I thought Blue and Cricket were one of the cutest things ever, but Sundew and</span>
  <span id="freeText15853628448028109822" style="display:none"><strong>I don’t even know where to start.</strong><br /><br />Okay, so first: the bad. <br />Whenever I first started this book, I was worried that it wouldn’t further the third arc’s plot quickly enough. By the end, though, it felt just a *teensy bit* too fast.<br />Also, Turtle didn’t get nearly as much spotlight as he deserved, but that’s just a nitpick coming from a Turtle fanboy.<br /><br />And that’s it! Onto the good:<br />SUNDEW AND WILLOW ARE SO FLIPPING ADORABLE! And I thought Blue and Cricket were one of the cutest things ever, but Sundew and Willow’s relationship is probably the most romantic and sweet one Tui has ever written. Definitely one of the highlights of the book. I would gush about it more, but there are other things to talk about.<br />Things happen! This may not come as a surprise to someone who is used to Wings of Fire, but as someone who has just finished reading the first two books of Warriors: TNP, this feels like a breath of fresh, forest air. I totally expected it to end when Sundew and her friends (and Nettle) found Hawthorn, but nope! The Wings of Fire universe was completely ripped open by the end. It was technically foreshadowed at the end of book 12, but I NEVER could’ve guessed the circumstances in which they would be leaving Pantala. Like Cricket, I have SO MANY QUESTIONS!<br />I loved the divide in the LeafWing tribe. The PoisonWings and SapWings didn’t just represent different mindsets among their leaders, but with it came misconceptions about the opposing tribes. The PoisonWings thought the SapWings were sappy, peace loving dragons (hence the name) that weren’t willing to do anything to stop the HiveWing oppression. So basically RainWings. And the SapWings believed that the PoisonWings were “offshoots” and perhaps a bit savage, with names based off of dangerous plants and pouches full of deadly weapons. However, as Sundew and Willow soon realized, they were both practically the same tribe, just with misunderstandings about each other. I love how Willow acts surprised at Sundew’s appearance when they first meet, as if she expected her to look like a dragon from a completely different tribe. There are more themes to cover, but that’s one of the big ones.<br />I also got the audiobook alongside the (delayed) Kindle release. I’d give Shannon’s performance 5 stars as well; though I’m not an expert in narration, I thought the majority of her performance was fantastic, with the only issues I had being nitpicks on how Cricket and Blue should sound (especially Cricket, though; I thought she sounded too cold when I expected her to sound warm and energetic).<br />There’s so much more to talk about with this book, but I don’t want this review to be too long. I want to keep this off the top of my head for the time being.<br /><br />In conclusion, if you like Wings of Fire, and you’ve been keeping up with the books, do not hesitate to buy this. You will adore it.<br />If you like Wings of Fire but haven’t been keeping up with the third arc, buy books 11 and 12 and then read book 13. It’s a good book on its own, but you’ll get a lot more out of it with some context.<br />If you haven’t read Wings of Fire, but you’re interested in this book, get the third arc if you’re inpatient; it doesn’t require very much context from the previous two. If you are patient, read the entire series and prepare to fall in love with these books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15853628448028109822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3495123876" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3495123876" />
    <a title="Lilliana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/111636381-lilliana"><img alt="Lilliana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598898523p2/111636381.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3495123876?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lilliana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lilliana" href="/user/show/111636381-lilliana">Lilliana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3495123876" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2401724761109996339">I'm going to start out with the bad.<br/>If you enjoy having overwhelming gay relationships shoved in your face this is the book for you. I absolutely HATE what the author did to sundew! She was independant, sassy, bossy, firery, and cool. Not a SOFT SAPPY ROMANTIC. Sundew's "relationship" with Willow was WAY.. to in-depth and weird. Other dragons, like Glory and Darkstalker had a funny, sarcastic, more.. less grossly sappy relationship. NOT touching, feeling, breathing. (BARF!) (Sorry got a bit carr</span>
  <span id="freeText2401724761109996339" style="display:none">I'm going to start out with the bad.<br />If you enjoy having overwhelming gay relationships shoved in your face this is the book for you. I absolutely HATE what the author did to sundew! She was independant, sassy, bossy, firery, and cool. Not a SOFT SAPPY ROMANTIC. Sundew's "relationship" with Willow was WAY.. to in-depth and weird. Other dragons, like Glory and Darkstalker had a funny, sarcastic, more.. less grossly sappy relationship. NOT touching, feeling, breathing. (BARF!) (Sorry got a bit carried away.) But you get the point. Children, like me should not have to be exposed to that. That completely RUINED MY LOVE FOR WINGS OF FIRE. Sigh.. that's super sad because I'm a HUGE Wings of fire fan! I own most of the books and have drawings of the dragons all over my room. But now..most of that is ruined. At one point when she was with Willow the book described it as"the most romantic thing ever" . REALLY? Also they met when they were two and Sundew said it was"love at first sight". I know dragons age faster than humans but still! AND love at first sight is not a thing. Sundew was a strong and loyal soldier who was mostly obedient to her parents. But in the Poison Jungle she was always arguing with her parents. And the way Sundew was always obsessing over Willow was not right. Other characters thought about the dragons they liked only a little bit, every once in a while, not constantly. It was to much. Everyone has there own opinions and that's fine but I did not appreciate having a same gender relationship shoved in my face. It is not the authors job to force this on us. As a Christian, same gender relationships are wrong. I feel very betrayed and stabbed in the back by this. It's very disappointing to see that Tui thinks she can force her opinion on me, she cannot. She should have thought about the fact that she was exposing CHILDREN to this. I am VERY DISCAPOINTED. Sundew's overwhelming gay relationship with Willow ruined most of the book for me. <br /><br />Another thing I didn't like is that Cricket, Sordtail, and Blue (Blue especially) we're kind of thrown aside. Sundew is so focused on Willow that Cricket, Sordtail, and Blue were ignored. <br /><br />In the first book the source of Wasps mind control is unknown. In the second book we figure out that Wasp uses a special plant and uses her tail stinger to mind control. Third book drops, and things start to get weird.The whole part with Hawthorn and the breath of evil was strange. The main bad guy went from Wasp ( witch was cool ) to a plant..... What a strange twist... Kinda disappointing if I'm being honest. Wasp was cooler, and now there's not really hope to save the hivewings. <br /><br />On to the good<br />The way the author described the Poison Jungle was amazing! It seemed so alive. She described it in such great detail. You could picture perfectly what the jungle looked and felt like. That part was great. The village also seems very cool. So.. basically the good was the description of the surroundings. <br /><br />I'm afraid that I didn't like this book. Wich again is SUPER SAD for me, as a wings of fire fan. I'm very disappointed in how this book turned out. And that completes my review of Wings of Fire Poison Jungle.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2401724761109996339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2936245607" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11151341444515653800">I enjoyed the Poison Jungle. I’ve been reading he WOF series for years now and I’ve loved every single book. However, I didn’t like this book as much as some of the other books in the series, such as Moon rising and The Hive Queen. I loved Bumblebee in this book. It was so cute how she called Sundew “Snudoo!” <br/> I didn’t enjoy Sundew’s point of view as much as some of the other protagonists. I didn’t love her personality and her backstory. <br/>I did really like Hazel and Willow, though. <br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a></span>
  <span id="freeText11151341444515653800" style="display:none">I enjoyed the Poison Jungle. I’ve been reading he WOF series for years now and I’ve loved every single book. However, I didn’t like this book as much as some of the other books in the series, such as Moon rising and The Hive Queen. I loved Bumblebee in this book. I am very excited to read book 14!! <br />I suspect that the protagonist will be Umber! :)</span>

<div id="review_2730709823" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2730709823" />
    <a title="GuineaPigFalconer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73657087-guineapigfalconer"><img alt="GuineaPigFalconer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510344418p2/73657087.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2730709823?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="GuineaPigFalconer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="GuineaPigFalconer" href="/user/show/73657087-guineapigfalconer">GuineaPigFalconer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781338214512" href="/book/show/41473825-the-poison-jungle">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2730709823&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2730709823" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11918776812177406086">This book was a short and fast read, but nonetheless just as enjoyable as the others! I really liked the character Sundew, and how her voice subtly shifted from the beginning of the book to the end. But I liked her adorable romance with Willow even more. <br/>The new setting of this book was fascinating, full of carnivorous plants - which I love anyways. There were also some great revelations and quite the cliffhanger!<br/>As for the epilogue, it's left me with a lot more questions than answers. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2837295405" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2837295405" />
    <a title="Noa Seidmann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21431012-noa-seidmann"><img alt="Noa Seidmann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533981865p2/21431012.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2837295405?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Noa Seidmann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Noa Seidmann" href="/user/show/21431012-noa-seidmann">Noa Seidmann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21431012-noa-seidmann?shelf=9-12">9-12</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2837295405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4834653634815011801">Tui T. Sutherland is one of the most amazing writers I have ever read. The 13th book of the series feel fresh and interesting as always. <br/>Blue, cricket, sundew and bumblebee get to the the poison jungle, where the leafwing dragons hide. War is coming. Our heroes discover a shocking secret, and again we end in a cliffhanger.<br/>Can't wait for the next one!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NAUfEHjOOIkKh6hXA7VjQTW0i7DjMXhr74P7pUIk+Dr68RhbS6FFQWFKy6Ed7Wq3N6fDr4G5+FGnPBqC5SfijQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KTcVX7z+3knw+YwG1jxAUZy9QM8vWB/6zluD9WLJVNjnwxIUj5GjgZs07/DIZEmnnq4I0E3Qn8CG5GLSxcpObw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7468669009583036579">Okay, I know what you’re thinking. Tui? What kind of name is that? Is it short for something?<br/><br/>Nope. Among the many great things to come out of New Zealand (the Lord of the Rings movies, cats that paint, my mom) is a bird called the tui—not as well known as the kiwi, but a heck of a lot noisier!<br/><br/>I was born July 31 (same birthday as Harry Potter!) in Caracas, Venezuela, and lived in Asuncion, Paraguay</span>
  <span id="freeText7468669009583036579" style="display:none">Okay, I know what you’re thinking. Tui? What kind of name is that? Is it short for something?<br /><br />Nope. Among the many great things to come out of New Zealand (the Lord of the Rings movies, cats that paint, my mom) is a bird called the tui—not as well known as the kiwi, but a heck of a lot noisier!<br /><br />I was born July 31 (same birthday as Harry Potter!) in Caracas, Venezuela, and lived in Asuncion, Paraguay; Miami, Florida; and Santo Domingo, Dominican Republic, before moving to New Jersey in high school, where I started doing theatre—mostly backstage work, because (a) it was fun, and (b) you got to hang out in the dark with cute boys. (Er, I mean . . . because it was artistically fulfilling, yes.)<br /><br />I graduated from Williams College in ’98 and I currently live in Boston with my husband, my perfect new baby, and my adorable yoodle Sunshine (what’s a yoodle? A puppy that’s three-quarters poodle and one-quarter Yorkshire terrier, of course!).<br /><br />Much to my parents’ relief, I abandoned my theatrical aspirations after college for the far more stable and lucrative career of fiction writing.<br /><br />My first two official books were beginning readers, part of Grosset &amp; Dunlap’s “First Friends” series for kids learning to read. MEET MO AND ELLA is tough to find now, but FUN WITH MO AND ELLA should still be out there somewhere.<br /><br />My first novel for teenagers was THIS MUST BE LOVE, which retells Shakespeare’s play A Midsummer Night’s Dream in a modern-day high school, from the POV of the two heroines, Hermia and Helena.<br /><br />And now I'm writing in a new project called SEEKERS! It's a children's book series that I'm writing with Erin Hunter. Check out my blog to find out more!</span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/57525496-the-poison-jungle-wings-of-fire-13">Quotes from The Poison Jungle</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;EKNO!” Bumblebee objected, throwing her arms around Cricket’s neck. “NOBYNOBYNOBE!” “That does look like fun,” Tsunami said wryly. “Bumblebee, be reasonable!” Cricket yelled over her wails. “There might be a war where I’m going! Dragons all stabbing each other! Very bad things! I don’t want you near that. I want you here and safe!” “STABEEBAD,” Bumblebee argued. “YUUUUsafe.” “I will be careful and I’ll come back soon. I promise.” She disentangled Bumblebee and the sling and handed them over to an extremely skeptical-looking Tsunami. “GROWLFACE!” the dragonet shouted. “ARGNORAW RGRUMPHLE!&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/10075938-ekno-bumblebee-objected-throwing-her-arms-around-cricket-s-neck-nobynobynobe">4 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Snudoo!” Bumblebee cheered. She lifted her little talons up and did a very good impression of something cute. Something more like a tamarin and definitely not like a HiveWing.&rdquo;</span>
